 ****************************************************************  125 1451   11
The new R-matrix analysis of the N-N system on which the ENDF/B-   125 1451   12
VII evaluation for 1H is based differs from the previous one use   125 1451   13
for ENDF/B-VI in several respects. Firstly, the n-p capture        125 1451   14
reaction (MT=102), and its inverse, deuteron photo-                125 1451   15
disintegration, were a part of the analysis, rather than added     125 1451   16
later as before. The analysis used a new method for including      125 1451   17
photon channels in R-matrix theory [1], which gave a better        125 1451   18
description of the E1 transitions, in particular.  The data for    125 1451   19
these reactions are mostly integrated and differential cross       125 1451   20
sections, but some information about polarizations was also        125 1451   21
included.  The thermal capture cross section was taken to be       125 1451   22
332.0 mb, as was the recommendation from preliminary data          125 1451   23
testing. Good agreement was obtained with recent cross-section     125 1451   24
measurements [2,3] by astrophysical groups in the 20-550 keV       125 1451   25
range, as well as with earlier measurements that had been done     125 1451   26
mostly as photo-disintegration experiments at energies below 14    125 1451   27
MeV.                                                               125 1451   28
The new analysis includes several additional measurements of the   125 1451   29
total cross section (MT=1).  The evaluated cross section           125 1451   30
deviates at most by about -0.5% around 10 MeV from that of         125 1451   31
ENDF/B-VI.  The estimated uncertainty of the MT=1 cross section    125 1451   32
is given at 2 MeV steps in the following table:                    125 1451   33
           En             Uncert. (%)                              125 1451   34
            0                0.20                                  125 1451   35
            2                0.22                                  125 1451   36
            4                0.30                                  125 1451   37
            6                0.36                                  125 1451   38
            8                0.44                                  125 1451   39
           10                0.50                                  125 1451   40
           12                0.49                                  125 1451   41
           14                0.46                                  125 1451   42
           16                0.40                                  125 1451   43
           18                0.35                                  125 1451   44
           20                0.30                                  125 1451   45
                                                                   125 1451   46
For n-p scattering (MT=2), new information was included about the  125 1451   47
low-energy cross sections (MF=3) and about the angular             125 1451   48
distributions (MF=4).  A new measurement of the angular            125 1451   49
distribution at 10 MeV [4], plus corrections to earlier data at    125 1451   50
14 MeV, moved the back-angle asymmetry in the 10-14 MeV range to   125 1451   51
values that lie between those obtained for ENDF/B-V and ENDF/B-    125 1451   52
VI.  The addition of the latest value of the thermal coherent      125 1451   53
scattering length [5] had the interesting effect of reducing the   125 1451   54
"zero-energy" scattering cross section somewhat to agree           125 1451   55
perfectly with an earlier measurement by Houk [6], and disagree    125 1451   56
with the later, more precise, value of Dilg [7].  The              125 1451   57
covariances for MT=2 will be added later, but the uncertainties    125 1451   58
on the integrated cross section should be similar to those         125 1451   59
listed above for the total cross section.                          125 1451   60
                                                                   125 1451   61

Covariances were adopted from COMMARA-2.0 library in July 2011.    125 1451   76
These covariances were obtained at LANL by full scale R-matrix     125 1451   77
analysis of more than 5000 experimental data (chi-square/degree    125 1451   78
of freedom of 0.83). [1] The major channel in this case is elastic 125 1451   79
scattering, often labeled also as ''n-p'' scattering. Elastic      125 1451   80
scattering serves as neutron cross section standard from 1 keV to  125 1451   81
20 MeV, with cross sections well determined. Uncertainties for     125 1451   82
elastic scattering rise from values well below 1%, reach maximum   125 1451   83
at about 8 MeV, then gradually decrease with increasing energy.    125 1451   84
In addition to elastic scattering, covariances are supplied for    125 1451   85
radiative capture.                                                 125 1451   86
                                                                   125 1451   87
REFERENCES                                                         125 1451   88
[1] G. M. Hale, "Covariances from light-element R-matrix           125 1451   89
analyses," Nuclear Data Sheets, 109, 2812 (2008).                  125 1451   90

The new R-matrix analysis of the N-N system on which the ENDF/B-   125 1451   12
VII evaluation for 1H is based differs from the previous one use   125 1451   13
for ENDF/B-VI in several respects. Firstly, the n-p capture        125 1451   14
reaction (MT=102), and its inverse, deuteron photo-                125 1451   15
disintegration, were a part of the analysis, rather than added     125 1451   16
later as before. The analysis used a new method for including      125 1451   17
photon channels in R-matrix theory [1], which gave a better        125 1451   18
description of the E1 transitions, in particular.  The data for    125 1451   19
these reactions are mostly integrated and differential cross       125 1451   20
sections, but some information about polarizations was also        125 1451   21
included.  The thermal capture cross section was taken to be       125 1451   22
332.0 mb, as was the recommendation from preliminary data          125 1451   23
testing. Good agreement was obtained with recent cross-section     125 1451   24
measurements [2,3] by astrophysical groups in the 20-550 keV       125 1451   25
range, as well as with earlier measurements that had been done     125 1451   26
mostly as photo-disintegration experiments at energies below 14    125 1451   27
MeV.                                                               125 1451   28
The new analysis includes several additional measurements of the   125 1451   29
total cross section (MT=1).  The evaluated cross section           125 1451   30
deviates at most by about -0.5% around 10 MeV from that of         125 1451   31
ENDF/B-VI.  The estimated uncertainty of the MT=1 cross section    125 1451   32
is given at 2 MeV steps in the following table:                    125 1451   33
           En             Uncert. (%)                              125 1451   34
            0                0.20                                  125 1451   35
            2                0.22                                  125 1451   36
            4                0.30                                  125 1451   37
            6                0.36                                  125 1451   38
            8                0.44                                  125 1451   39
           10                0.50                                  125 1451   40
           12                0.49                                  125 1451   41
           14                0.46                                  125 1451   42
           16                0.40                                  125 1451   43
           18                0.35                                  125 1451   44
           20                0.30                                  125 1451   45
                                                                   125 1451   46
For n-p scattering (MT=2), new information was included about the  125 1451   47
low-energy cross sections (MF=3) and about the angular             125 1451   48
distributions (MF=4).  A new measurement of the angular            125 1451   49
distribution at 10 MeV [4], plus corrections to earlier data at    125 1451   50
14 MeV, moved the back-angle asymmetry in the 10-14 MeV range to   125 1451   51
values that lie between those obtained for ENDF/B-V and ENDF/B-    125 1451   52
VI.  The addition of the latest value of the thermal coherent      125 1451   53
scattering length [5] had the interesting effect of reducing the   125 1451   54
"zero-energy" scattering cross section somewhat to agree           125 1451   55
perfectly with an earlier measurement by Houk [6], and disagree    125 1451   56
with the later, more precise, value of Dilg [7].  The              125 1451   57
covariances for MT=2 will be added later, but the uncertainties    125 1451   58
on the integrated cross section should be similar to those         125 1451   59
listed above for the total cross section.                          125 1451   60
                                                                   125 1451   61

Covariances were adopted from COMMARA-2.0 library in July 2011.    125 1451   76
These covariances were obtained at LANL by full scale R-matrix     125 1451   77
analysis of more than 5000 experimental data (chi-square/degree    125 1451   78
of freedom of 0.83). [1] The major channel in this case is elastic 125 1451   79
scattering, often labeled also as ''n-p'' scattering. Elastic      125 1451   80
scattering serves as neutron cross section standard from 1 keV to  125 1451   81
20 MeV, with cross sections well determined. Uncertainties for     125 1451   82
elastic scattering rise from values well below 1%, reach maximum   125 1451   83
at about 8 MeV, then gradually decrease with increasing energy.    125 1451   84
In addition to elastic scattering, covariances are supplied for    125 1451   85
radiative capture.                                                 125 1451   86

 ****************************************************************  125 1451   11
The new R-matrix analysis of the N-N system on which the ENDF/B-   125 1451   12
VII evaluation for 1H is based differs from the previous one use   125 1451   13
for ENDF/B-VI in several respects. Firstly, the n-p capture        125 1451   14
reaction (MT=102), and its inverse, deuteron photo-                125 1451   15
disintegration, were a part of the analysis, rather than added     125 1451   16
later as before. The analysis used a new method for including      125 1451   17
photon channels in R-matrix theory [1], which gave a better        125 1451   18
description of the E1 transitions, in particular.  The data for    125 1451   19
these reactions are mostly integrated and differential cross       125 1451   20
sections, but some information about polarizations was also        125 1451   21
included.  The thermal capture cross section was taken to be       125 1451   22
332.0 mb, as was the recommendation from preliminary data          125 1451   23
testing. Good agreement was obtained with recent cross-section     125 1451   24
measurements [2,3] by astrophysical groups in the 20-550 keV       125 1451   25
range, as well as with earlier measurements that had been done     125 1451   26
mostly as photo-disintegration experiments at energies below 14    125 1451   27
MeV.                                                               125 1451   28
The new analysis includes several additional measurements of the   125 1451   29
total cross section (MT=1).  The evaluated cross section           125 1451   30
deviates at most by about -0.5% around 10 MeV from that of         125 1451   31
ENDF/B-VI.  The estimated uncertainty of the MT=1 cross section    125 1451   32
is given at 2 MeV steps in the following table:                    125 1451   33
           En             Uncert. (%)                              125 1451   34
            0                0.20                                  125 1451   35
            2                0.22                                  125 1451   36
            4                0.30                                  125 1451   37
            6                0.36                                  125 1451   38
            8                0.44                                  125 1451   39
           10                0.50                                  125 1451   40
           12                0.49                                  125 1451   41
           14                0.46                                  125 1451   42
           16                0.40                                  125 1451   43
           18                0.35                                  125 1451   44
           20                0.30                                  125 1451   45
                                                                   125 1451   46
For n-p scattering (MT=2), new information was included about the  125 1451   47
low-energy cross sections (MF=3) and about the angular             125 1451   48
distributions (MF=4).  A new measurement of the angular            125 1451   49
distribution at 10 MeV [4], plus corrections to earlier data at    125 1451   50
14 MeV, moved the back-angle asymmetry in the 10-14 MeV range to   125 1451   51
values that lie between those obtained for ENDF/B-V and ENDF/B-    125 1451   52
VI.  The addition of the latest value of the thermal coherent      125 1451   53
scattering length [5] had the interesting effect of reducing the   125 1451   54
"zero-energy" scattering cross section somewhat to agree           125 1451   55
perfectly with an earlier measurement by Houk [6], and disagree    125 1451   56
with the later, more precise, value of Dilg [7].  The              125 1451   57
covariances for MT=2 will be added later, but the uncertainties    125 1451   58
on the integrated cross section should be similar to those         125 1451   59
listed above for the total cross section.                          125 1451   60
                                                                   125 1451   61
REFERENCES                                                         125 1451   62
                                                                   125 1451   63
[1] G. M. Hale and A. S. Johnson, Proc. 17th Int. IUPAP Conf. on   125 1451   64
    Few-Body Problems in Physics, 5-10 June 2003, Durham NC, W.    125 1451   65
    Gloeckle and W. Tornow,  eds., Elsevier B.V., pp. S120-S122    125 1451   66
   (2004).                                                         125 1451   67
[2] T. S. Suzuki et al., Astrophys. Lett. 449, L59 (1995).         125 1451   68
[3] Y. Nagai et al., Phys. Rev. C 56, 3173 (1997).                 125 1451   69
[4] N. Boukharouba et al., Phys. Rev. C 65, 014004 (2002).         125 1451   70
[5] K. Schoen et al., Phys. Rev. C 67, 044005 (2003).              125 1451   71
[6] T. L. Houk, Phys. Rev. C 3, 1886 (1971).                       125 1451   72
[7] W. Dilg, Phys. Rev. C 11, 103 (1975).                          125 1451   73
 ****************************************************************  125 1451   74
                                                                   125 1451   75
Covariances were adopted from COMMARA-2.0 library in July 2011.    125 1451   76
These covariances were obtained at LANL by full scale R-matrix     125 1451   77
analysis of more than 5000 experimental data (chi-square/degree    125 1451   78
of freedom of 0.83). [1] The major channel in this case is elastic 125 1451   79
scattering, often labeled also as ''n-p'' scattering. Elastic      125 1451   80
scattering serves as neutron cross section standard from 1 keV to  125 1451   81
20 MeV, with cross sections well determined. Uncertainties for     125 1451   82
elastic scattering rise from values well below 1%, reach maximum   125 1451   83
at about 8 MeV, then gradually decrease with increasing energy.    125 1451   84
In addition to elastic scattering, covariances are supplied for    125 1451   85
radiative capture.                                                 125 1451   86
                                                                   125 1451   87
REFERENCES                                                         125 1451   88
[1] G. M. Hale, "Covariances from light-element R-matrix           125 1451   89
analyses," Nuclear Data Sheets, 109, 2812 (2008).                  125 1451   90

           16                0.40                                  125 1451   43
           18                0.35                                  125 1451   44
           20                0.30                                  125 1451   45
                                                                   125 1451   46
For n-p scattering (MT=2), new information was included about the  125 1451   47
low-energy cross sections (MF=3) and about the angular             125 1451   48
distributions (MF=4).  A new measurement of the angular            125 1451   49
distribution at 10 MeV [4], plus corrections to earlier data at    125 1451   50
14 MeV, moved the back-angle asymmetry in the 10-14 MeV range to   125 1451   51
values that lie between those obtained for ENDF/B-V and ENDF/B-    125 1451   52
VI.  The addition of the latest value of the thermal coherent      125 1451   53
scattering length [5] had the interesting effect of reducing the   125 1451   54
"zero-energy" scattering cross section somewhat to agree           125 1451   55
perfectly with an earlier measurement by Houk [6], and disagree    125 1451   56
with the later, more precise, value of Dilg [7].  The              125 1451   57
covariances for MT=2 will be added later, but the uncertainties    125 1451   58
on the integrated cross section should be similar to those         125 1451   59
listed above for the total cross section.                          125 1451   60
                                                                   125 1451   61

                                                                   125 1451   75
Covariances were adopted from COMMARA-2.0 library in July 2011.    125 1451   76
These covariances were obtained at LANL by full scale R-matrix     125 1451   77
analysis of more than 5000 experimental data (chi-square/degree    125 1451   78
of freedom of 0.83). [1] The major channel in this case is elastic 125 1451   79
scattering, often labeled also as ''n-p'' scattering. Elastic      125 1451   80
scattering serves as neutron cross section standard from 1 keV to  125 1451   81
20 MeV, with cross sections well determined. Uncertainties for     125 1451   82
elastic scattering rise from values well below 1%, reach maximum   125 1451   83
at about 8 MeV, then gradually decrease with increasing energy.    125 1451   84
In addition to elastic scattering, covariances are supplied for    125 1451   85
radiative capture.                                                 125 1451   86
                                                                   125 1451   87

analyses," Nuclear Data Sheets, 109, 2812 (2008).                  125 1451   90

 ENDF/B-VI MOD 4 Revision, February 1998, G. M. Hale and           125 1451   36
           P. G. Young (LANL)                                      125 1451   37
                                                                   125 1451   38
    This is an update of the ENDF/B-VI evaluation to extend the    125 1451   39
 incident neutron energy range from 100 to 150 MeV.  The elastic   125 1451   40
 scattering cross section from the R-matrix analysis used for      125 1451   41
 ENDF/B-VI is matched in the energy region of 26 - 30 MeV to       125 1451   42
 elastic cross sections from Arndt's phase-shift solution, Vol.40. 125 1451   43
 Arndt's elastic cross section is used directly in the evaluation  125 1451   44
 above the matching region to 150 MeV.  A smooth extrapolation was 125 1451   45
 made of MT=102 to 150 MeV.                                        125 1451   46
    This new evaluation has a smoother transition across the       125 1451   47
 matching region than did the previous ENDF/B-VI file, and         125 1451   48
 corresponds more closely to the recommendation of the EANDC       125 1451   49
 standards subcommittee for n-p cross sections above 20 MeV.       125 1451   50
 Proton kerma values calculated from this file deviate by no more  125 1451   51
 than 2% from the previous ENDF/B-VI values at energies up to 100  125 1451   52
 MeV.                                                              125 1451   53
                                                                   125 1451   54
 ***************************************************************** 125 1451   55
                                                                   125 1451   56

    The cross section for radiative capture at thermal was         125 1451   59
 changed to the ENDF/B-V value (from 0.3326 to 0.3320 b), with     125 1451   60
 appropriate changes at lower energies for 1/v behavior.  The      125 1451   61
 total cross section was slightly decreased to accomodate this     125 1451   62
 change in radiative capture.                                      125 1451   63

 ENDF/B-VI MOD 1 Evaluation, October 1989, G.M. Hale,              125 1451   75
                 D.C. Dodder, E.R. Siciliano, W.B. Wilson (LANL)   125 1451   76
                                                                   125 1451   77
    This is a completely new evaluation independent of ENDF/B-V,   125 1451   78
 except as noted below.                                            125 1451   79
     Elastic cross sections and angular distributions below 40 MeV 125 1451   80
 were determined with a new R-Matrix calculation by Hale and       125 1451   81
 Dodder.  This calculation gives the ENDF/B-VI elastic scattering  125 1451   82
 cross sections for hydrogen below 20 MeV.  Also, elastic cross    125 1451   83
 sections and angular distributions above 20 MeV were calculated   125 1451   84
 with the npscat code using phase shifts of Arndt by Siciliano and 125 1451   85
 Wilson.                                                           125 1451   86
    Angular distributions at 26 MeV agreed well: below this energy 125 1451   87
 R-Matrix angular distributions were used; at and above 26 MeV     125 1451   88
 phase shift angular distributions were used.                      125 1451   89
    Elastic cross sections below 26 MeV were taken from the        125 1451   90
 R-Matrix work; those above 30 MeV were taken from the phase shift 125 1451   91
 work.  Between these energies the elastic cross section was taken 125 1451   92
 as follows:                                                       125 1451   93
                                                                   125 1451   94
      E (eV)       R-Matrix     Phase shift     MF3MT2             125 1451   95
     ----------   ----------   -------------   ---------           125 1451   96
      2.6E+07      0.36345         0.36029      0.36345            125 1451   97
      2.7E+07      0.34859                      0.34811            125 1451   98
      2.8E+07      0.33488         0.33104      0.33295            125 1451   99
      2.9E+07      0.32227                      0.31891            125 1451  100
      3.0E+07      0.31080         0.30567      0.30567            125 1451  101
                                                                   125 1451  102
    These calculated results were merged with available (n,gamma)  125 1451  103
 data by Wilson.  ENDF/B-V (n,gamma) data were used below 20 MeV;  125 1451  104
 above this energy, an approximation to the data of M. Bosman et   125 1451  105
 al. [Bo79] was used.                                              125 1451  106
    The (n,gamma) was adjusted to agree exactly with Mughabghab    125 1451  107
 [Mu81] value at thermal (0.3326 b), and lower energies were       125 1451  108
 modified according to 1/v law (P. Young, 10/17/89).  The total    125 1451  109
 cross section was then summed again to reflect the revised        125 1451  110
 (n,gamma).                                                        125 1451  111
                                                                   125 1451  112
    File 2, MT151 resonance parameters were taken from ENDF/B-V.   125 1451  113
                                                                   125 1451  114
    File 12 and File 14, MT102 are also taken from ENDF/B-V.       125 1451  115

 STANDARDS COVARIANCES                                             125 1451  118
                                                                   125 1451  119
 Phase 1 reviewers of the ENDF/B-VI standards cross sections have  125 1451  120
 expressed the concern that the uncertainties resulting from the   125 1451  121
 combination of R-matrix and simultaneous evaluations might have   125 1451  122
 led to uncertainties that are too small.  As a result, the        125 1451  123
 Standards Subcommittee produced (at the May, 1990 CSEWG meeting)  125 1451  124
 a set of expanded covariance estimates for the standard cross     125 1451  125
 section reactions.  These uncertainties are estimates such that   125 1451  126
 if a modern day experiment were performed on a given standard     125 1451  127
 cross section using the best techniques, approximately 2/3 of     125 1451  128
 the results should fall within these expanded uncertainties. The  125 1451  129
 expanded uncertainties for the n + H-1 total cross section are    125 1451  130
 as follows:                                                       125 1451  131
                                                                   125 1451  132
    Energy Range (keV)    Estimated Uncertainty (%)                125 1451  133
    ------------------    -------------------------                125 1451  134
     1.0E-08 - 20000                0.2                            125 1451  135
                                                                   125 1451  136
 ----------------------------------------------------------------- 125 1451  137

 ENDF/B-VI MOD 5 Revision, Jan. 2001, S.C. Frankle and P.G. Young  125 1451   23
                 (LANL)                                            125 1451   24
                                                                   125 1451   25
    The energy of the photon from neutron capture (MT=102) in      125 1451   26
 File 12 has been updated to 2.2233 MeV.                           125 1451   27

 ****************************************************************  125 1451   29
                                                                   125 1451   30
 ENDF/B-VI MOD 4 Revision, February 1998, G. M. Hale and           125 1451   31
           P. G. Young (LANL)                                      125 1451   32
                                                                   125 1451   33
    This is an update of the ENDF/B-VI evaluation to extend the    125 1451   34
 incident neutron energy range from 100 to 150 MeV.  The elastic   125 1451   35
 scattering cross section from the R-matrix analysis used for      125 1451   36
 ENDF/B-VI is matched in the energy region of 26 - 30 MeV to       125 1451   37
 elastic cross sections from Arndt's phase-shift solution, Vol.40. 125 1451   38
 Arndt's elastic cross section is used directly in the evaluation  125 1451   39
 above the matching region to 150 MeV.  A smooth extrapolation was 125 1451   40
 made of MT=102 to 150 MeV.                                        125 1451   41
    This new evaluation has a smoother transition across the       125 1451   42
 matching region than did the previous ENDF/B-VI file, and         125 1451   43
 corresponds more closely to the recommendation of the EANDC       125 1451   44
 standards subcommittee for n-p cross sections above 20 MeV.       125 1451   45
 Proton kerma values calculated from this file deviate by no more  125 1451   46
 than 2% from the previous ENDF/B-VI values at energies up to 100  125 1451   47
 MeV.                                                              125 1451   48
                                                                   125 1451   49
 ***************************************************************** 125 1451   50
                                                                   125 1451   51
 ENDF/B-VI MOD 3 Revision, October 1997, P.G. Young (LANL)         125 1451   52
                                                                   125 1451   53
    The cross section for radiative capture at thermal was         125 1451   54
 changed to the ENDF/B-V value (from 0.3326 to 0.3320 b), with     125 1451   55
 appropriate changes at lower energies for 1/v behavior.  The      125 1451   56
 total cross section was slightly decreased to accomodate this     125 1451   57
 change in radiative capture.                                      125 1451   58
                                                                   125 1451   59
 ***************************************************************** 125 1451   60
                                                                   125 1451   61
 ENDF/B-VI MOD 2 Revision, July 1991                               125 1451   62
                                                                   125 1451   63
    The only revision was to add to the description of the         125 1451   64
 ENDF/B-VI evaluation, given below, the comments on the standards  125 1451   65
 covariances.                                                      125 1451   66
                                                                   125 1451   67
 ***************************************************************** 125 1451   68
                                                                   125 1451   69
 ENDF/B-VI MOD 1 Evaluation, October 1989, G.M. Hale,              125 1451   70
                 D.C. Dodder, E.R. Siciliano, W.B. Wilson (LANL)   125 1451   71
                                                                   125 1451   72
    This is a completely new evaluation independent of ENDF/B-V,   125 1451   73
 except as noted below.                                            125 1451   74
     Elastic cross sections and angular distributions below 40 MeV 125 1451   75
 were determined with a new R-Matrix calculation by Hale and       125 1451   76
 Dodder.  This calculation gives the ENDF/B-VI elastic scattering  125 1451   77
 cross sections for hydrogen below 20 MeV.  Also, elastic cross    125 1451   78
 sections and angular distributions above 20 MeV were calculated   125 1451   79
 with the npscat code using phase shifts of Arndt by Siciliano and 125 1451   80
 Wilson.                                                           125 1451   81
    Angular distributions at 26 MeV agreed well: below this energy 125 1451   82
 R-Matrix angular distributions were used; at and above 26 MeV     125 1451   83
 phase shift angular distributions were used.                      125 1451   84
    Elastic cross sections below 26 MeV were taken from the        125 1451   85
 R-Matrix work; those above 30 MeV were taken from the phase shift 125 1451   86
 work.  Between these energies the elastic cross section was taken 125 1451   87
 as follows:                                                       125 1451   88
                                                                   125 1451   89
      E (eV)       R-Matrix     Phase shift     MF3MT2             125 1451   90
     ----------   ----------   -------------   ---------           125 1451   91
      2.6E+07      0.36345         0.36029      0.36345            125 1451   92
      2.7E+07      0.34859                      0.34811            125 1451   93
      2.8E+07      0.33488         0.33104      0.33295            125 1451   94
      2.9E+07      0.32227                      0.31891            125 1451   95
      3.0E+07      0.31080         0.30567      0.30567            125 1451   96
                                                                   125 1451   97
    These calculated results were merged with available (n,gamma)  125 1451   98
 data by Wilson.  ENDF/B-V (n,gamma) data were used below 20 MeV;  125 1451   99
 above this energy, an approximation to the data of M. Bosman et   125 1451  100
 al. [Bo79] was used.                                              125 1451  101
    The (n,gamma) was adjusted to agree exactly with Mughabghab    125 1451  102
 [Mu81] value at thermal (0.3326 b), and lower energies were       125 1451  103
 modified according to 1/v law (P. Young, 10/17/89).  The total    125 1451  104
 cross section was then summed again to reflect the revised        125 1451  105
 (n,gamma).                                                        125 1451  106
                                                                   125 1451  107
    File 2, MT151 resonance parameters were taken from ENDF/B-V.   125 1451  108
                                                                   125 1451  109
    File 12 and File 14, MT102 are also taken from ENDF/B-V.       125 1451  110
                                                                   125 1451  111

 STANDARDS COVARIANCES                                             125 1451  113
                                                                   125 1451  114
 Phase 1 reviewers of the ENDF/B-VI standards cross sections have  125 1451  115
 expressed the concern that the uncertainties resulting from the   125 1451  116
 combination of R-matrix and simultaneous evaluations might have   125 1451  117
 led to uncertainties that are too small.  As a result, the        125 1451  118
 Standards Subcommittee produced (at the May, 1990 CSEWG meeting)  125 1451  119
 a set of expanded covariance estimates for the standard cross     125 1451  120
 section reactions.  These uncertainties are estimates such that   125 1451  121
 if a modern day experiment were performed on a given standard     125 1451  122
 cross section using the best techniques, approximately 2/3 of     125 1451  123
 the results should fall within these expanded uncertainties. The  125 1451  124
 expanded uncertainties for the n + H-1 total cross section are    125 1451  125
 as follows:                                                       125 1451  126
                                                                   125 1451  127
    Energy Range (keV)    Estimated Uncertainty (%)                125 1451  128
    ------------------    -------------------------                125 1451  129
     1.0E-08 - 20000                0.2                            125 1451  130
                                                                   125 1451  131
 ----------------------------------------------------------------- 125 1451  132

HISTORY                                                            125 1451   11
08-07  All data were taken from ENDF/B-VII.0.                      125 1451   12
       Compiled by K.Shibata (jaea).                               125 1451   13

         2200m/s Sig (b)        res. integ. (b) [0.5 to 2.0e+7 eV] 125 1451   16
 total      20.768                  -                              125 1451   17
 elastic    20.436                  -                              125 1451   18
 capture     0.332                0.1492                           125 1451   19
****************************************************************** 125 1451   20
                                                                   125 1451   21
 ****************************************************************  125 1451   22
The new R-matrix analysis of the N-N system on which the ENDF/B-   125 1451   23
VII evaluation for 1H is based differs from the previous one use   125 1451   24
for ENDF/B-VI in several respects. Firstly, the n-p capture        125 1451   25
reaction (MT=102), and its inverse, deuteron photo-                125 1451   26
disintegration, were a part of the analysis, rather than added     125 1451   27
later as before. The analysis used a new method for including      125 1451   28
photon channels in R-matrix theory [1], which gave a better        125 1451   29
description of the E1 transitions, in particular.  The data for    125 1451   30
these reactions are mostly integrated and differential cross       125 1451   31
sections, but some information about polarizations was also        125 1451   32
included.  The thermal capture cross section was taken to be       125 1451   33
332.0 mb, as was the recommendation from preliminary data          125 1451   34
testing. Good agreement was obtained with recent cross-section     125 1451   35
measurements [2,3] by astrophysical groups in the 20-550 keV       125 1451   36
range, as well as with earlier measurements that had been done     125 1451   37
mostly as photo-disintegration experiments at energies below 14    125 1451   38
MeV.                                                               125 1451   39
The new analysis includes several additional measurements of the   125 1451   40
total cross section (MT=1).  The evaluated cross section           125 1451   41
deviates at most by about -0.5% around 10 MeV from that of         125 1451   42
ENDF/B-VI.  The estimated uncertainty of the MT=1 cross section    125 1451   43
is given at 2 MeV steps in the following table:                    125 1451   44
           En             Uncert. (%)                              125 1451   45
            0                0.20                                  125 1451   46
            2                0.22                                  125 1451   47
            4                0.30                                  125 1451   48
            6                0.36                                  125 1451   49
            8                0.44                                  125 1451   50
           10                0.50                                  125 1451   51
           12                0.49                                  125 1451   52
           14                0.46                                  125 1451   53
           16                0.40                                  125 1451   54
           18                0.35                                  125 1451   55
           20                0.30                                  125 1451   56
                                                                   125 1451   57
For n-p scattering (MT=2), new information was included about the  125 1451   58
low-energy cross sections (MF=3) and about the angular             125 1451   59
distributions (MF=4).  A new measurement of the angular            125 1451   60
distribution at 10 MeV [4], plus corrections to earlier data at    125 1451   61
14 MeV, moved the back-angle asymmetry in the 10-14 MeV range to   125 1451   62
values that lie between those obtained for ENDF/B-V and ENDF/B-    125 1451   63
VI.  The addition of the latest value of the thermal coherent      125 1451   64
scattering length [5] had the interesting effect of reducing the   125 1451   65
"zero-energy" scattering cross section somewhat to agree           125 1451   66
perfectly with an earlier measurement by Houk [6], and disagree    125 1451   67
with the later, more precise, value of Dilg [7].  The              125 1451   68
covariances for MT=2 will be added later, but the uncertainties    125 1451   69
on the integrated cross section should be similar to those         125 1451   70
listed above for the total cross section.                          125 1451   71
                                                                   125 1451   72

                                                                   125 1451   12
 ENDF/B-VI MOD 5 Revision, Jan. 2001, S.C. Frankle and P.G. Young  125 1451   13
                 (LANL)                                            125 1451   14
                                                                   125 1451   15
    The energy of the photon from neutron capture (MT=102) in      125 1451   16
 File 12 has been updated to 2.2233 MeV.                           125 1451   17
                                                                   125 1451   18
 ****************************************************************  125 1451   19
                                                                   125 1451   20
 ENDF/B-VI MOD 4 Revision, February 1998, G. M. Hale and           125 1451   21
           P. G. Young (LANL)                                      125 1451   22
                                                                   125 1451   23
    This is an update of the ENDF/B-VI evaluation to extend the    125 1451   24
 incident neutron energy range from 100 to 150 MeV.  The elastic   125 1451   25
 scattering cross section from the R-matrix analysis used for      125 1451   26
 ENDF/B-VI is matched in the energy region of 26 - 30 MeV to       125 1451   27
 elastic cross sections from Arndt's phase-shift solution, Vol.40. 125 1451   28
 Arndt's elastic cross section is used directly in the evaluation  125 1451   29
 above the matching region to 150 MeV.  A smooth extrapolation was 125 1451   30
 made of MT=102 to 150 MeV.                                        125 1451   31
    This new evaluation has a smoother transition across the       125 1451   32
 matching region than did the previous ENDF/B-VI file, and         125 1451   33
 corresponds more closely to the recommendation of the EANDC       125 1451   34
 standards subcommittee for n-p cross sections above 20 MeV.       125 1451   35
 Proton kerma values calculated from this file deviate by no more  125 1451   36
 than 2% from the previous ENDF/B-VI values at energies up to 100  125 1451   37
 MeV.                                                              125 1451   38
                                                                   125 1451   39
 ***************************************************************** 125 1451   40
                                                                   125 1451   41
 ENDF/B-VI MOD 3 Revision, October 1997, P.G. Young (LANL)         125 1451   42
                                                                   125 1451   43
    The cross section for radiative capture at thermal was         125 1451   44
 changed to the ENDF/B-V value (from 0.3326 to 0.3320 b), with     125 1451   45
 appropriate changes at lower energies for 1/v behavior.  The      125 1451   46
 total cross section was slightly decreased to accomodate this     125 1451   47
 change in radiative capture.                                      125 1451   48
                                                                   125 1451   49
 ***************************************************************** 125 1451   50
                                                                   125 1451   51
 ENDF/B-VI MOD 2 Revision, July 1991                               125 1451   52
                                                                   125 1451   53
    The only revision was to add to the description of the         125 1451   54
 ENDF/B-VI evaluation, given below, the comments on the standards  125 1451   55
 covariances.                                                      125 1451   56
                                                                   125 1451   57
 ***************************************************************** 125 1451   58
                                                                   125 1451   59
 ENDF/B-VI MOD 1 Evaluation, October 1989, G.M. Hale,              125 1451   60
                 D.C. Dodder, E.R. Siciliano, W.B. Wilson (LANL)   125 1451   61
                                                                   125 1451   62
    This is a completely new evaluation independent of ENDF/B-V,   125 1451   63
 except as noted below.                                            125 1451   64
     Elastic cross sections and angular distributions below 40 MeV 125 1451   65
 were determined with a new R-Matrix calculation by Hale and       125 1451   66
 Dodder.  This calculation gives the ENDF/B-VI elastic scattering  125 1451   67
 cross sections for hydrogen below 20 MeV.  Also, elastic cross    125 1451   68
 sections and angular distributions above 20 MeV were calculated   125 1451   69
 with the npscat code using phase shifts of Arndt by Siciliano and 125 1451   70
 Wilson.                                                           125 1451   71
    Angular distributions at 26 MeV agreed well: below this energy 125 1451   72
 R-Matrix angular distributions were used; at and above 26 MeV     125 1451   73
 phase shift angular distributions were used.                      125 1451   74
    Elastic cross sections below 26 MeV were taken from the        125 1451   75
 R-Matrix work; those above 30 MeV were taken from the phase shift 125 1451   76
 work.  Between these energies the elastic cross section was taken 125 1451   77
 as follows:                                                       125 1451   78
                                                                   125 1451   79
      E (eV)       R-Matrix     Phase shift     MF3MT2             125 1451   80
     ----------   ----------   -------------   ---------           125 1451   81
      2.6E+07      0.36345         0.36029      0.36345            125 1451   82
      2.7E+07      0.34859                      0.34811            125 1451   83
      2.8E+07      0.33488         0.33104      0.33295            125 1451   84
      2.9E+07      0.32227                      0.31891            125 1451   85
      3.0E+07      0.31080         0.30567      0.30567            125 1451   86
                                                                   125 1451   87
    These calculated results were merged with available (n,gamma)  125 1451   88
 data by Wilson.  ENDF/B-V (n,gamma) data were used below 20 MeV;  125 1451   89
 above this energy, an approximation to the data of M. Bosman et   125 1451   90
 al. [Bo79] was used.                                              125 1451   91
    The (n,gamma) was adjusted to agree exactly with Mughabghab    125 1451   92
 [Mu81] value at thermal (0.3326 b), and lower energies were       125 1451   93
 modified according to 1/v law (P. Young, 10/17/89).  The total    125 1451   94
 cross section was then summed again to reflect the revised        125 1451   95
 (n,gamma).                                                        125 1451   96
                                                                   125 1451   97
    File 2, MT151 resonance parameters were taken from ENDF/B-V.   125 1451   98
                                                                   125 1451   99
    File 12 and File 14, MT102 are also taken from ENDF/B-V.       125 1451  100
                                                                   125 1451  101
 ----------------------------------------------------------------- 125 1451  102
 STANDARDS COVARIANCES                                             125 1451  103
                                                                   125 1451  104
 Phase 1 reviewers of the ENDF/B-VI standards cross sections have  125 1451  105
 expressed the concern that the uncertainties resulting from the   125 1451  106
 combination of R-matrix and simultaneous evaluations might have   125 1451  107
 led to uncertainties that are too small.  As a result, the        125 1451  108
 Standards Subcommittee produced (at the May, 1990 CSEWG meeting)  125 1451  109
 a set of expanded covariance estimates for the standard cross     125 1451  110
 section reactions.  These uncertainties are estimates such that   125 1451  111
 if a modern day experiment were performed on a given standard     125 1451  112
 cross section using the best techniques, approximately 2/3 of     125 1451  113
 the results should fall within these expanded uncertainties. The  125 1451  114
 expanded uncertainties for the n + H-1 total cross section are    125 1451  115
 as follows:                                                       125 1451  116
                                                                   125 1451  117
    Energy Range (keV)    Estimated Uncertainty (%)                125 1451  118
    ------------------    -------------------------                125 1451  119
     1.0E-08 - 20000                0.2                            125 1451  120
                                                                   125 1451  121
 ----------------------------------------------------------------- 125 1451  122

  National Laboratory report, LA-UR-99-1222 (1999)                 125 1451  127
[Mu81]  S.F. Mughabghab, M. Divadeenam, and N.E. Holden, Neutron   125 1451  128
    Cross Sections, Vol. 1, Neutron Resonance Parameters and       125 1451  129
    Thermal Cross Sections (Academic Press, 1981).                 125 1451  130

 ****************************************************************  125 1451   11
 Comments by V. Pronyaev to the revision of ENDF/B-VII.1:          125 1451   12
 1H(n,n) is a basic standard and at least the central values of    125 1451   13
 this cross section should be the same in all libraries.           125 1451   14
 G. Hale R-matrix (EDA) evaluation for ENDF/B-VII.1 evaluated for  125 1451   15
 standards was taken as a base for one correction. It concerns the 125 1451   16
 uncertainty of the standard.                                      125 1451   17
 Original EDA (calculations) of CS uncertainties from uncertaint.  125 1451   18
 of adjusted parameters gives extremely low uncertainties because  125 1451   19
 normalization of experimental data in the fit are considered as   125 1451   20
 free. Then due to strong cancellation of statistical              125 1451   21
 uncertainties we have very low total evaluated uncertainties.     125 1451   22
 In 2008 the procedure of calculations of covariance matrices of   125 1451   23
 from covariance matrix of parameters was changed, and as result   125 1451   24
 the total evaluated uncertainties are substantially larger        125 1451   25
 CSEWG (1991) experts estimation of total uncertainty for 1H(n,n). 125 1451   26
 Unfortunately CSEWG had not prepared the covariance (correlation) 125 1451   27
 matrix, but consider CSEWG estimates as only statistical is not   125 1451   28
 right.                                                            125 1451   29
 This file contains in MF=33, MT=2 the CSEWG (1991) percent        125 1451   30
 estimates of total uncertainties and covariance matrix, obtained  125 1451   31
 from 2 components - statistical and systematical fully correlated 125 1451   32
 in all energy range - 1.0e-5 eV to 20 MeV. Systematical           125 1451   33
 was taken equalto 0.18% what is at 0.02% below total in low-      125 1451   34
 energy part where because of 1/v dependence and large number of   125 1451   35
 points the uncertainties are minimal. The obtained covariance     125 1451   36
 matrix is semi-positive and has three 0 eigenvalues               125 1451   37
****************************************************************   125 1451   38
The new R-matrix analysis of the N-N system on which the ENDF/B-   125 1451   39
VII evaluation for 1H is based differs from the previous one use   125 1451   40
for ENDF/B-VI in several respects. Firstly, the n-p capture        125 1451   41
reaction (MT=102), and its inverse, deuteron photo-                125 1451   42
disintegration, were a part of the analysis, rather than added     125 1451   43
later as before. The analysis used a new method for including      125 1451   44
photon channels in R-matrix theory [1], which gave a better        125 1451   45
description of the E1 transitions, in particular.  The data for    125 1451   46
these reactions are mostly integrated and differential cross       125 1451   47
sections, but some information about polarizations was also        125 1451   48
included.  The thermal capture cross section was taken to be       125 1451   49
332.0 mb, as was the recommendation from preliminary data          125 1451   50
testing. Good agreement was obtained with recent cross-section     125 1451   51
measurements [2,3] by astrophysical groups in the 20-550 keV       125 1451   52
range, as well as with earlier measurements that had been done     125 1451   53
mostly as photo-disintegration experiments at energies below 14    125 1451   54
MeV.                                                               125 1451   55
The new analysis includes several additional measurements of the   125 1451   56
total cross section (MT=1).  The evaluated cross section           125 1451   57
deviates at most by about -0.5% around 10 MeV from that of         125 1451   58
ENDF/B-VI.  The estimated uncertainty of the MT=1 cross section    125 1451   59
is given at 2 MeV steps in the following table:                    125 1451   60
           En             Uncert. (%)                              125 1451   61
            0                0.20                                  125 1451   62
            2                0.22                                  125 1451   63
            4                0.30                                  125 1451   64
            6                0.36                                  125 1451   65
            8                0.44                                  125 1451   66
           10                0.50                                  125 1451   67
           12                0.49                                  125 1451   68
           14                0.46                                  125 1451   69
           16                0.40                                  125 1451   70
           18                0.35                                  125 1451   71
           20                0.30                                  125 1451   72
                                                                   125 1451   73
For n-p scattering (MT=2), new information was included about the  125 1451   74
low-energy cross sections (MF=3) and about the angular             125 1451   75
distributions (MF=4).  A new measurement of the angular            125 1451   76
distribution at 10 MeV [4], plus corrections to earlier data at    125 1451   77
14 MeV, moved the back-angle asymmetry in the 10-14 MeV range to   125 1451   78
values that lie between those obtained for ENDF/B-V and ENDF/B-    125 1451   79
VI.  The addition of the latest value of the thermal coherent      125 1451   80
scattering length [5] had the interesting effect of reducing the   125 1451   81
"zero-energy" scattering cross section somewhat to agree           125 1451   82
perfectly with an earlier measurement by Houk [6], and disagree    125 1451   83
with the later, more precise, value of Dilg [7].  The              125 1451   84
covariances for MT=2 will be added later, but the uncertainties    125 1451   85
on the integrated cross section should be similar to those         125 1451   86
listed above for the total cross section.                          125 1451   87
                                                                   125 1451   88

                                                                   125 1451  102
Covariances were adopted from COMMARA-2.0 library in July 2011.    125 1451  103
These covariances were obtained at LANL by full scale R-matrix     125 1451  104
analysis of more than 5000 experimental data (chi-square/degree    125 1451  105
of freedom of 0.83). [1] The major channel in this case is elastic 125 1451  106
scattering, often labeled also as ''n-p'' scattering. Elastic      125 1451  107
scattering serves as neutron cross section standard from 1 keV to  125 1451  108
20 MeV, with cross sections well determined. Uncertainties for     125 1451  109
elastic scattering rise from values well below 1%, reach maximum   125 1451  110
at about 8 MeV, then gradually decrease with increasing energy.    125 1451  111
In addition to elastic scattering, covariances are supplied for    125 1451  112
radiative capture.                                                 125 1451  113
                                                                   125 1451  114
REFERENCES                                                         125 1451  115
[1] G. M. Hale, "Covariances from light-element R-matrix           125 1451  116
analyses," Nuclear Data Sheets, 109, 2812 (2008).                  125 1451  117

  1-H -  1 LANL       EVAL-OCT05 G.M.Hale                          101 1451   27

 ****************************************************************  101 1451   30
The new R-matrix analysis of the N-N system on which the ENDF/B-   101 1451   31
VII evaluation for 1H is based differs from the previous one use   101 1451   32
for ENDF/B-VI in several respects. Firstly, the n-p capture        101 1451   33
reaction (MT=102), and its inverse, deuteron photo-                101 1451   34
disintegration, were a part of the analysis, rather than added     101 1451   35
later as before. The analysis used a new method for including      101 1451   36
photon channels in R-matrix theory [1], which gave a better        101 1451   37
description of the E1 transitions, in particular.  The data for    101 1451   38
these reactions are mostly integrated and differential cross       101 1451   39
sections, but some information about polarizations was also        101 1451   40
included.  The thermal capture cross section was taken to be       101 1451   41
332.0 mb, as was the recommendation from preliminary data          101 1451   42
testing. Good agreement was obtained with recent cross-section     101 1451   43
measurements [2,3] by astrophysical groups in the 20-550 keV       101 1451   44
range, as well as with earlier measurements that had been done     101 1451   45
mostly as photo-disintegration experiments at energies below 14    101 1451   46
MeV.                                                               101 1451   47
The new analysis includes several additional measurements of the   101 1451   48
total cross section (MT=1).  The evaluated cross section           101 1451   49
deviates at most by about -0.5% around 10 MeV from that of         101 1451   50
ENDF/B-VI.  The estimated uncertainty of the MT=1 cross section    101 1451   51
is given at 2 MeV steps in the following table:                    101 1451   52
           En             Uncert. (%)                              101 1451   53
            0                0.20                                  101 1451   54
            2                0.22                                  101 1451   55
            4                0.30                                  101 1451   56
            6                0.36                                  101 1451   57
            8                0.44                                  101 1451   58
           10                0.50                                  101 1451   59
           12                0.49                                  101 1451   60
           14                0.46                                  101 1451   61
           16                0.40                                  101 1451   62
           18                0.35                                  101 1451   63
           20                0.30                                  101 1451   64
                                                                   101 1451   65
For n-p scattering (MT=2), new information was included about the  101 1451   66
low-energy cross sections (MF=3) and about the angular             101 1451   67
distributions (MF=4).  A new measurement of the angular            101 1451   68
distribution at 10 MeV [4], plus corrections to earlier data at    101 1451   69
14 MeV, moved the back-angle asymmetry in the 10-14 MeV range to   101 1451   70
values that lie between those obtained for ENDF/B-V and ENDF/B-    101 1451   71
VI.  The addition of the latest value of the thermal coherent      101 1451   72
scattering length [5] had the interesting effect of reducing the   101 1451   73
"zero-energy" scattering cross section somewhat to agree           101 1451   74
perfectly with an earlier measurement by Houk [6], and disagree    101 1451   75
with the later, more precise, value of Dilg [7].  The              101 1451   76
covariances for MT=2 will be added later, but the uncertainties    101 1451   77
on the integrated cross section should be similar to those         101 1451   78
listed above for the total cross section.                          101 1451   79
                                                                   101 1451   80

           10                0.50                                  101 1451   59
           12                0.49                                  101 1451   60
           14                0.46                                  101 1451   61
           16                0.40                                  101 1451   62
           18                0.35                                  101 1451   63
           20                0.30                                  101 1451   64
                                                                   101 1451   65
For n-p scattering (MT=2), new information was included about the  101 1451   66
low-energy cross sections (MF=3) and about the angular             101 1451   67
distributions (MF=4).  A new measurement of the angular            101 1451   68
distribution at 10 MeV [4], plus corrections to earlier data at    101 1451   69
14 MeV, moved the back-angle asymmetry in the 10-14 MeV range to   101 1451   70
values that lie between those obtained for ENDF/B-V and ENDF/B-    101 1451   71
VI.  The addition of the latest value of the thermal coherent      101 1451   72
scattering length [5] had the interesting effect of reducing the   101 1451   73
"zero-energy" scattering cross section somewhat to agree           101 1451   74
perfectly with an earlier measurement by Houk [6], and disagree    101 1451   75
with the later, more precise, value of Dilg [7].  The              101 1451   76
covariances for MT=2 will be added later, but the uncertainties    101 1451   77
on the integrated cross section should be similar to those         101 1451   78
listed above for the total cross section.                          101 1451   79
                                                                   101 1451   80

   this is a completely new evaluation independent of endf/b-v,    125 1451   34
       except as noted below.                                      125 1451   35
     elastic cross sections and angular distributions below        125 1451   36
       30 mev were determined with a new r-matrix                  125 1451   37
       calculation by hale and dodder. this calculation gives      125 1451   38
       the endf/b-vi elastic scattering cross sections for         125 1451   39
       hydrogen below 20 mev.                                      125 1451   40
     also, elastic cross sections and angular distributions above  125 1451   41
       20 mev were calculated with the npscat code using phase     125 1451   42
       shifts of arndt by siciliano and wilson.                    125 1451   43
     angular distributions at 26 mev agreed well: below this       125 1451   44
       energy r-matrix angular distributions were used; at and     125 1451   45
       above 26 mev phase shift angular distributions were used.   125 1451   46
     elastic cross sections below 26 mev were taken from the       125 1451   47
       r-matrix work; those above 30 mev were taken from the       125 1451   48
       phase shift work.  between these energies the elastic       125 1451   49
       cross section was taken as follows:                         125 1451   50
                                                                   125 1451   51
                 e (ev)      r-matrix      phase shift    mf3mt2   125 1451   52
               ----------   -----------  -------------- ---------- 125 1451   53
                2.6e+07      .36345          .36029       .36345   125 1451   54
                2.7e+07      .34859                       .34811   125 1451   55
                2.8e+07      .33488          .33104       .33295   125 1451   56
                2.9e+07      .32227                       .31891   125 1451   57
                3.0e+07      .31080          .30567       .30567   125 1451   58
                                                                   125 1451   59
                                                                   125 1451   60
     These calculated results were merged with available n-gamma   125 1451   61
         data by wilson. endf/b-v (n,gamma) data were used below   125 1451   62
         20 mev; above this energy, an approximation to the data   125 1451   63
         of M. Bosman et al.(phys.lett.82b,212[1979]) was used.    125 1451   64
     The (n,gamma) was adjusted to agree exactly with Mughabghab   125 1451   65
         (1983) value at thermal (0.3326 b), and lower energies    125 1451   66
         were modified according to 1/v law (P. Young, 10/17/89).  125 1451   67
         The total cross section was then summed again to reflect  125 1451   68
         the revised (n,gamma).                                    125 1451   69

                        STANDARDS COVARIANCES                      125 1451   78
                                                                   125 1451   79
 Phase 1 reviewers of the ENDF/B-VI standards cross sections have  125 1451   80
 expressed the concern that the uncertainties resulting from the   125 1451   81
 combination of R-matrix and simultaneous evaluations might have   125 1451   82
 led to uncertainties that are too small.  As a result, the        125 1451   83
 Standards Subcommittee produced (at the May, 1990 CSEWG meeting)  125 1451   84
 a set of expanded covariance estimates for the standard cross     125 1451   85
 section reactions.  These uncertainties are estimates such that   125 1451   86
 if a modern day experiment were performed on a given standard     125 1451   87
 cross section using the best techniques, approximately 2/3 of     125 1451   88
 the results should fall within these expanded uncertainties. The  125 1451   89
 expanded uncertainties for the n + H-1 total cross section are    125 1451   90
 as follows:                                                       125 1451   91

 ****************************************************************  125 1451   11
The new R-matrix analysis of the N-N system on which the ENDF/B-   125 1451   12
VII evaluation for 1H is based differs from the previous one use   125 1451   13
for ENDF/B-VI in several respects. Firstly, the n-p capture        125 1451   14
reaction (MT=102), and its inverse, deuteron photo-                125 1451   15
disintegration, were a part of the analysis, rather than added     125 1451   16
later as before. The analysis used a new method for including      125 1451   17
photon channels in R-matrix theory [1], which gave a better        125 1451   18
description of the E1 transitions, in particular.  The data for    125 1451   19
these reactions are mostly integrated and differential cross       125 1451   20
sections, but some information about polarizations was also        125 1451   21
included.  The thermal capture cross section was taken to be       125 1451   22
332.0 mb, as was the recommendation from preliminary data          125 1451   23
testing. Good agreement was obtained with recent cross-section     125 1451   24
measurements [2,3] by astrophysical groups in the 20-550 keV       125 1451   25
range, as well as with earlier measurements that had been done     125 1451   26
mostly as photo-disintegration experiments at energies below 14    125 1451   27
MeV.                                                               125 1451   28
The new analysis includes several additional measurements of the   125 1451   29
total cross section (MT=1).  The evaluated cross section           125 1451   30
deviates at most by about -0.5% around 10 MeV from that of         125 1451   31
ENDF/B-VI.  The estimated uncertainty of the MT=1 cross section    125 1451   32
is given at 2 MeV steps in the following table:                    125 1451   33
           En             Uncert. (%)                              125 1451   34
            0                0.20                                  125 1451   35
            2                0.22                                  125 1451   36
            4                0.30                                  125 1451   37
            6                0.36                                  125 1451   38
            8                0.44                                  125 1451   39
           10                0.50                                  125 1451   40
           12                0.49                                  125 1451   41
           14                0.46                                  125 1451   42
           16                0.40                                  125 1451   43
           18                0.35                                  125 1451   44
           20                0.30                                  125 1451   45
                                                                   125 1451   46
For n-p scattering (MT=2), new information was included about the  125 1451   47
low-energy cross sections (MF=3) and about the angular             125 1451   48
distributions (MF=4).  A new measurement of the angular            125 1451   49
distribution at 10 MeV [4], plus corrections to earlier data at    125 1451   50
14 MeV, moved the back-angle asymmetry in the 10-14 MeV range to   125 1451   51
values that lie between those obtained for ENDF/B-V and ENDF/B-    125 1451   52
VI.  The addition of the latest value of the thermal coherent      125 1451   53
scattering length [5] had the interesting effect of reducing the   125 1451   54
"zero-energy" scattering cross section somewhat to agree           125 1451   55
perfectly with an earlier measurement by Houk [6], and disagree    125 1451   56
with the later, more precise, value of Dilg [7].  The              125 1451   57
covariances for MT=2 will be added later, but the uncertainties    125 1451   58
on the integrated cross section should be similar to those         125 1451   59
listed above for the total cross section.                          125 1451   60
                                                                   125 1451   61

 ****************************************************************  125 1451   74
                                                                   125 1451   75
Covariances were adopted from COMMARA-2.0 library in July 2011.    125 1451   76
These covariances were obtained at LANL by full scale R-matrix     125 1451   77
analysis of more than 5000 experimental data (chi-square/degree    125 1451   78
of freedom of 0.83). [1] The major channel in this case is elastic 125 1451   79
scattering, often labeled also as ''n-p'' scattering. Elastic      125 1451   80
scattering serves as neutron cross section standard from 1 keV to  125 1451   81
20 MeV, with cross sections well determined. Uncertainties for     125 1451   82
elastic scattering rise from values well below 1%, reach maximum   125 1451   83
at about 8 MeV, then gradually decrease with increasing energy.    125 1451   84
In addition to elastic scattering, covariances are supplied for    125 1451   85
radiative capture.                                                 125 1451   86

analyses," Nuclear Data Sheets, 109, 2812 (2008).                  125 1451   90
